Page 13

International Problems Research Association Invited Dr. Liang Yunli to Give a Lecture Yesterday 133

Recent Developments in International Affairs and the Sino-Japanese Incident

Dr. Liang Yunli, former Special Commissioner to the League of Nations Assembly and current Councilor of the Executive Yuan of the National Government, was invited by the Shanghai International Problems Research Association to give a lecture at the association at 5:00 PM yesterday (the 8th) on his recent impressions in Geneva. The following is a record of his speech:

Last year, I gave a speech in the United States on the international political and legal significance of the Sino-Japanese problem. In October, our delegation, with the Lytton Report, submitted it to the special assembly to be held in November for discussion. The international situation became increasingly tense. There were many aspects of the problem of the Northeastern Provinces that needed legal clarification, so I specifically telegraphed the United States inviting me to go to Geneva to assist. I arrived in Geneva in mid-November, at which time the League of Nations Executive Yuan was preparing to begin its meeting. People from various countries who were interested in international problems flocked to Geneva to observe. Since the Treaty of Versailles, there has been no international political event that has attracted more attention from experts and the general public than this one. This is not only because whether the League of Nations can continue to prolong its existence depends on the resolution of the Northeastern Provinces Incident, but also because whether the global movement for peace and anti-war that has spread throughout the world since the Great War has any significance and needs to continue depends on whether the Japanese can be sanctioned by world opinion as a touchstone. From my personal perspective, the heated attention given to the Northeastern Provinces Incident in terms of public opinion is far greater than that received by the governments of various countries. Most governments (especially the governments of the so-called "Great Powers") have the mentality of appeasement, turning big problems into small ones, and small problems into nothing, because their own practical interests have not been severely damaged by this. The statements made by British Foreign Secretary Simon and French Foreign Minister Peng Gu all recognized the Northeastern Provinces Incident as a local incident, with no direct relationship to general world politics. But this is their external rhetoric. In fact, they are engaged in a power struggle, and their attempts to exempt Japan from responsibility have never ceased. Simon, on the one hand, insisted at the disarmament conference that Germany should abide by the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant regarding military reduction, and on the other hand, excused Japan's actions in violating the Covenant. The obvious contradiction in his policy is obvious to all. However, in order to conceal his contradiction, Simon greatly advocated the theory that Japan's military actions in China were not "war" in the sense of international law. In fact, the views of international legal scholars on this point have changed greatly. What Simon advocates is only a one-sided view, with purely political reasons behind it, and is not accepted by new-school jurists. The indifference of the great powers towards the Northeastern Provinces Incident has remained unchanged. Although the special assembly passed the report of the Committee of Nineteen this spring, this resolute measure of the League of Nations to condemn Japan should not be said to be a change in the attitude of the great powers of Britain and France, but rather a result of pressure from world public opinion. In Britain, France, and especially the United States, all institutions that study international problems, such as our International Problems Research Association, are deeply sorry for the incompetence of the League of Nations. Among them, there are also clear expressions that they will stop supporting the League of Nations if the League of Nations dares not even impose theoretical and moral sanctions on Japan. For example, the British League of Nations Association (a private organization) and the American Foreign Policy Association (also a private organization) have all made clear statements regarding Japan's violation of the Covenant. This is a clear phenomenon in international politics, and can give us a sense of comfort.

The achievements of our delegation in Geneva over the past year have been disclosed in the newspapers from time to time, so I won't repeat them here. After the assembly passed the report of the Committee of Nineteen in February of this year, the atmosphere in Geneva changed from tension to depression. Although there was a disarmament conference, from the perspective of the Sino-Japanese Incident, the effectiveness of the League of Nations seemed to have ended here. I recently heard that the report of the "Advisory Committee" established by the assembly on not recognizing "Manchukuo" has been published. All newspapers have published it in recent days, but this report will definitely not have the effect we hope for if it is not followed by the economic sanctions stipulated in Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant. Apart from the principle of "non-recognition," which only has a slight force in the negative aspect, it is of no help in stopping aggression. Moreover, as time passes, the great powers are obsessed with their own interests, and even this principle may not be strictly adhered to. Recently, there have been news of Japanese bandits invading North China. At this time of military tension, it is ridiculous to only engage in the formulation of negative principles.

My personal view is that our country should always advocate submitting Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant at an appropriate time. Some say that in order to submit this article, our country must declare war or break off diplomatic relations. I believe that from a purely legal point of view, these two conditions are not necessary. What Article 16 prohibits is "acts of war" rather than a "state of war." Some international jurists make a distinction between "acts" and "states." I believe that the fundamental concept of modern international law tends towards the dynamic aspect, focusing on the control of various acts, rather than the consistency of abstract logic. What the Covenant prohibits is actual acts of war, not the state of war recognized by traditional international law. I have discussed this issue many times. On my way back to China, I wrote an article for the August issue of "Shen Bao Monthly," which also pointed out the misunderstanding of this point by the general public.

Because of the weakness of the League of Nations in handling the Northeastern Provinces Incident, it has turned its attention to engaging in technical cooperation with our country. This may not be "losing mulberry in the east but gaining it in the west." The function of the League of Nations is divided into two parts: one is to prevent war, and the other is to promote cooperation. The former is more difficult, and the latter is easier. But if the latter has remarkable results, the existence of the League of Nations has considerable justification. We should not have great expectations for international organizations. Our policy should be to exhaust the effectiveness of these opportunities. All countries attach considerable importance to the League of Nations. Conducting diplomacy in Geneva does not mean that weak countries have no chance of success. In 1924 and 1925, Germany's power had declined to the extreme, but because of the resourceful means and far-sightedness of Foreign Minister Stresemann in Geneva, Germany was invited to join the League of Nations in 1926, and its international status also improved rapidly. Currently, all important countries have diplomats with high qualifications and prestige permanently stationed in Geneva. I believe that if our country wants to continue Geneva diplomacy, it should choose those with a global perspective and specialized knowledge of international politics to be permanently stationed there to interact with the representatives of Britain and France. Mr. Wu Tiyun had repeatedly expressed this idea when he was the representative. I believe that the International Problems Research Association should find ways to connect with organizations with the same goals in Britain and the United States in order to achieve the goal of effectively influencing international public opinion. US Senator Borah said that in order for government actions to be effective, public opinion must be constantly whipped. If there are unsatisfactory aspects of international organizations, we should not hesitate to whip them to make them aware of the need for caution. I hope that the International Problems Research Association can use its whips frequently.

Frederick Maze Went to North China the Day Before Yesterday 134

Wang Gongjue's Troops Telegraph Heavy Fighting Against the Japanese 136

Lacking Food and Ammunition, Besieged

The Shanghai Liaison Office of the Third Route Army of the Northeastern Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army recently received a telegram from its commander, Wang Gongjue, stating that the First and Second Southern Detachments are currently stationed in Jing'an Fort, Feng Wang Kou, Yongning Cheng and its vicinity near Chicheng, holding key positions for defense. Suddenly, two enemy planes came and dropped eight bombs, but only three exploded. The Detachment Commander Wan Kecheng shot down an injured enemy plane with a Russian-style machine gun. That night at dawn, the enemy launched a large-scale attack, intending to eliminate our army. The troops of the First Detachment, Yang Zhifu's department, fought bravely, fighting fiercely for two days and nights, but the enemy did not succeed. Due to the lack of food and ammunition, the enemy took the opportunity to surround them, and the situation was very intense. They telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Zhu for instructions. During the hand-to-hand combat, they personally led the Broadsword Team and the Special Service Detachment, taking the enemy's rear road, and broke through the encirclement. In this battle, our army suffered more than 300 casualties, including the death of Company Commander Wu Changtai, Company Adjutant Zhong Qi, Zhang Desheng, Zuo Dacai, and Platoon Leader Li Shilin, Chen Shizhong, Hu Ying, and Jin Qichang. The enemy also suffered heavy casualties and captured more than 70 rifles, five automatic rifles, and one heavy machine gun. They are now jointly defending with Yin Bohong's department of the Fifth Route Army to resist the enemy's attack.

Hu Xiyuan Requests Establishment of a Tungsten Refining Plant 137

A Document Presented to the Ministry of Industry

Tungsten is tough, not easily dissolved, and a very important mineral in modern industry. When refined into wire, it emits light when an electric current is passed through it, and can replace the platinum wire used in the past. Therefore, it is a basic raw material for the manufacture of light bulbs. China is very rich in tungsten, but the Chinese people do not know how to refine it, so they rely on foreigners and lose their rights to profits. Recently, the Ministry of Industry of our country has established a Tungsten Mine Production and Sales Bureau, but it only pays attention to the export of raw materials and does not try to refine it itself. Hu Xiyuan, General Manager of China Yabu Er Electric Appliance Factory, noting the difficulty and danger that China cannot refine tungsten itself, specifically submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating the importance of refining tungsten wire by itself. Excerpts from the original text are as follows: (Omitted above) I have found that tungsten wire is the main raw material for various weapons, machinery, and electrical appliances. China produces 80% of the world's tungsten, and the output of the Gan Nan region alone accounts for 10% of the country. Because the Chinese people have not set up factories for refining, foreigners buy raw materials every year, and after they are refined in their countries, they are sold back to China. The quantity recorded in the customs import register is shocking, and the national foundation is in danger. Recently, I read a report that your Ministry has a proposal to establish a Tungsten Mine Production and Sales Bureau, so the production and sales channels will be supervised and guided, and there will be a path to follow, and the exploitation of profit sources is deeply admirable. However, with such abundant production and such important raw materials, if we do not set up factories to refine them ourselves, then we still have to rely on foreigners for military equipment and industrial manufacturing. With one transfer between export and import, foreigners enjoy the profits, and China's losses are huge. Once there is a war, the source is cut off, and not only will industrial manufacturing be extremely difficult, but I am afraid that military equipment will not be able to be rescued. Thinking of this, I am terrified. The plan for now is to make preparations in advance. I would like to ask your Ministry to plan to set up factories and establish a century-long plan for a fundamental solution. The beginning is certainly difficult, but one effort can be permanent. (Omitted below) and so on.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegram to Ministry of Finance Requesting Exemption from Supplementary Tobacco Tax 138

Supporting Cotton Yarn Consolidated Tax Precedent to Issue Inventory Certificates

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, saying: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: This Chamber received a letter on the 7th of this month from the Tobacco Trade Association, stating that since 1930, the tobacco industry has been in decline, with inventories piling up and unable to be sold. As of now, there are still 16,500 unsold cases of aged domestic tobacco leaves stored in this port, mainly from Anhui's Susong, Henan's Dengxian, Jiangxi's Guangfeng, Zhejiang's Xinchang, Tongxiang, and Hubei's Huanggang and Yunxian. The reasons for the stagnation of sales are roughly as follows: (1) The cigarette tax was changed from a three-tier system to a two-tier system. Cigarette factories found it unprofitable to produce low-grade cigarettes and switched to producing mid-grade cigarettes. Aged tobacco leaves were previously used as raw materials for low-grade cigarettes. Since cigarette factories stopped producing low-grade cigarettes, aged tobacco leaves could not be sold. (2) Domestic tobacco leaves were once popular in the Northeast and Korea. Since the September 18th Incident, the Northeast has been occupied, industry and commerce have ceased, and war has raged. The tobacco business in that area has been completely cut off. Tobacco leaves previously shipped to Korea now have to pass through Dalian into the puppet state via Shanghai due to the seizure of the Northeast Customs by the puppet state. The customs duties require five or six taels per picul of tobacco leaves, making it uneconomical due to price concerns, so no one is buying. (3) Foreign countries have increased import duties on tobacco leaves and encouraged people to grow tobacco to resist the import of Chinese tobacco. Therefore, in recent years, foreign firms have experienced very slow business. These domestic tobacco leaves, accumulated over the years, have changed in quality due to prolonged storage, and their prices have plummeted. Added to this are storage rent and all other expenses, resulting in huge losses. In recent years, some businesses in the industry have closed down due to economic pressure, and some have gone bankrupt due to excessive losses. Even those who are fortunate enough to barely maintain their operations are in a state of hardship that cannot be described in words. The Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance has now promulgated regulations on special taxes for domestic tobacco leaves, stipulating that if domestic tobacco leaves stored in this port are transported to other ports, new taxes must be paid, and the old taxes already paid will be refunded. However, the old tobacco sales fees vary from province to province, but are all lower than the current new tax of 4.15 yuan per 100 catties. According to the regulations of the tax authorities, the more expensive tobacco leaves will have to pay an additional five or six yuan in new taxes per picul, and the cheaper ones will have to pay seven or eight jiao. Our industry, after years of losses, really cannot bear any further burden. We propose that your association appeal to the tax authorities to give special consideration to the difficulties of businesses and maintain the tobacco industry. For aged domestic tobacco leaves on which public sales fees have already been paid, whether sold in this port or shipped for export, we request that no new taxes be levied and that the Tax Bureau issue aged tobacco sales and transportation certificates for identification and facilitating sales. We respectfully request your association's vigorous assistance and thorough arrangements, which will be appreciated by all." Upon arrival at the association, it was found that the industry's accumulated tobacco leaves were all due to sluggish sales and inability to sell, and the storage rent and interest paid over the years were already considerable. If they are again required to pay the newly promulgated special tax with a higher tax rate and refund the public sales fee with a lower rate, then merchants will suffer another loss between the payment and the refund. Moreover, as with the initial implementation of the consolidated tax on cotton yarn, there was a deadline for clearing inventory, and inventory certificates were issued upon export to exempt them from the consolidated tax. It seems inappropriate to be uniquely biased against the special tax on tobacco leaves. We hereby submit a telegram to your esteemed ministry for review and approval, requesting that you grant the association's request to issue certificates for the transportation and sale of stored tobacco leaves and exempt them from the special tax, which would be in the public interest. respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Chinese Medical Association Presents to Legislative Yuan President Sun 139

Requesting the Rejection of the National Medical Institute Regulations

The Chinese Medical Association yesterday submitted a presentation to the Legislative Yuan regarding the National Medical Institute and the Ministry of Health, stating: "Presenting a request: It is found that China's medical facilities have long lagged behind, and the annual mortality rate is several times higher than that of advanced countries in the East and West. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it has regarded improving public health as an important task and established a special Ministry of Health to manage national medical administration. Although the ministry was later changed to a department, the scope of administration and its efficiency have not been reduced as a result. Since the establishment of the central health administrative organ, health construction has been carried out without reservation. Here, the association will present to your esteemed Yuan the most obvious examples. During the floods of the year before last, the Battle of Shanghai last year, and the war in North China this spring, health personnel participated in every battle, and many were saved by epidemic prevention and rescue. When epidemics spread in various provinces and cities, the Ministry of Health and local organs cooperated closely, and each achieved success. In addition, the establishment of central hospitals, the dissemination of health knowledge, the establishment of medical management, and the efforts to awaken the public are all obvious to everyone. It is not easy to achieve such results in a short period of time. However, in July of the 20th year, the Central National Medical Institute was established, with the aim of reorganizing and improving national medicine using scientific methods. However, in the two years since then, there has not been the slightest improvement in national medicine, and suddenly a regulation on the management of national medicine has been formed, which is ridiculous. The association, upon hearing this, earnestly believes that it is not possible. Central administration should have unified organs. Departments such as education and transportation each have specialized duties, and departments and sections are set up to cooperate and form a system. Hygiene management is no exception. In the past, Japanese Han medicine and Western medicine were opposed to each other. The government advocated science, weighed the pros and cons, and also used those who conformed to science to administer. Now, if our country wants to manage new doctors as one organ and old doctors as another, it will be like building a house on top of another house. How can we unify power? If the National Medical Institute is truly scientific, then the Ministry of Health should be abolished, and national health and medicine should be managed by the National Medical Institute. If the Ministry of Health is scientific, then the National Medical Institute should be abolished, and national health and medicine should be managed by the Ministry of Health. Moreover, the National Medical Institute itself also admits that it is unscientific, because its purpose is to use scientific methods to reorganize and improve our country's inherent medicine, which shows that it does not conform to science and wants to be scientific. Whether it can be transformed is still a question. Even if it does, it should be subordinate to the scientific Ministry of Health for improvement. It should not blindly use a non-scientific group to hope to become scientific, so that it can be a separate system. Let's take the so-called improved national medicine as an example. Some people learn anatomy in school, some people learn physiology, some people use Western methods to inject when they start a business, and some people use thermometers. Are they Chinese or Western? Will they be managed by the National Medical Institute or by the Ministry of Health? Or will a third organ be set up to manage them? Let's take Chinese medicine as an example. Chinese medicine such as ephedra is boiled with boiling water as a Chinese method, and its components are extracted as a Western method, but its effects are the same. Then, such as rhubarb, boiled with boiling water is a Chinese method, and extracted with alcohol and water is a Western method. To the extent of exhausting the categories, there is no end. May I ask whether these medicines should be managed by the National Medical Institute or by the Ministry of Health? Or will a third organ be set up to manage them? Conflicts of authority, unclear boundaries, hygiene management, a mess. The simultaneous existence of a non-scientific organ and a scientific organ introduces a detour when the national people's concept of science is still young and fragile. What is the danger? The association's heart is in danger, and it dare not speak. We respectfully request that your esteemed Yuan examine the facts, weigh the pros and cons, and reject the National Medical Institute Regulations, and not allow its establishment. The future of hygiene depends on it. This presentation is to Sun, President of the Legislative Yuan. Niu Huisheng, President of the Chinese Medical Association."

Various Wine Industry Associations Appeal for Amendments to the New System 140

Slight Increase in Burden Endured Painfully

Strict Regulations Vowed Not to Be Recognized

The local yellow wine, Shaoxing wine, sauce wine, Liang shochu, and sauce garden trade associations in this city, all feeling that the tax bureau's implementation of the fixed tax on local wine is oppressing business and making it impossible to maintain operations, have successively announced the suspension of remittances and brewing. The joint meeting decided the day before yesterday to submit a letter to party and government organs, the All-China Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Joint Association, and the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, appealing for amendments. The original text is recorded as follows: "Presenting a statement clarifying that the new tax on local wine is too burdensome, causing various industries to suffer oppression and suspend transportation and brewing, respectfully requesting your esteemed meeting and bureau to quickly request amendments to eliminate disputes and maintain business. The member associations and other trades have been paying wine tax for various types of wine for many years, nominally as public sales fees, levied at 20% of the value, with production taxes collected separately in two places. Local wine without sales behavior is not taxed in advance, which has been convenient for merchants and people for nearly 20 years. However, since July 1st of this year, the tax bureau has changed the regulations, abolished public sales, and separately stipulated a fixed tax on local wine, totaling eight chapters and forty articles. The articles are burdensome, the procedures are cumbersome, the penalty rules are severe, and manufacturers must pay full taxes on wine in storage that is not involved in sales and obtain a tax certificate, otherwise it will be treated as private production and sales, confiscated, and severely punished. The various industries feel oppressed and unable to maintain operations. Forced to do so, the member associations of Shaoxing wine, local yellow wine, and sauce wine have successively suspended transportation and brewing after voting by the members' congress to show their determination. The member associations of Liang shochu and sauce gardens, feeling that the lips are cold when the teeth are lost, can only continue to convene members' congresses to make representations, which are generally nothing more than shutting down. The implementation of this new tax is indeed annihilating business. The member associations solicited opinions from members, who all agreed that a slight increase in the burden could be endured painfully, but they vowed not to recognize the strict regulations. Moreover, the cancellation of the special stamp for local yellow wine (i.e., half-tax stamp) is cutting off livelihoods and is particularly severe. The overall attitude is consistent. Therefore, the member associations are of the opinion that the new regulations should be amended as appropriate so that the tax is fair and business is convenient, those who have suspended operations can resume operations, and those who have not suspended operations can be at peace. The advantages and disadvantages are obvious. In addition to submitting a presentation to the Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Department, we hereby submit a presentation with the association's seal, respectfully requesting that your esteemed chairman examine and verify, uphold justice, and request that the tax authorities amend the new regulations as appropriate, announce them to all, so as to eliminate disputes and maintain business, for which we will be extremely grateful."

Gu Hongsheng attempted to rescue him, and Liu Mingshan also fell into the river. Later, dockworkers rescued Gu, but they were unable to rescue Liu, who died. The body has now been recovered and examined by the prosecutor, who found no injuries on Liu's body, indicating that he died from drowning. The police department believes the defendant is suspected of negligence causing death and is now prosecuting him under Article 291 of the criminal law, requesting the court to investigate, etc.

Photographs of the scene taken by the police were also presented to the court. The judge asked Russian Constable No. 91 how Liu Mingshan fell into the river.

The constable replied that he was patrolling Huangpu Bund that night with No. 64 and Chinese constables.

Turning South and Returning North 155

They saw floating, on the wharf,

many people, gambling

and arguing, so they immediately

went forward together to expel them, shouting at them to disperse from about ten steps away. Then he saw the victim tripped by a rope or iron chain on a pile and fell into the river. Asked if he had gone to capture them, he replied that he was more than twenty feet away and only shouted. They fell down while fleeing. Asked Constable Sun Hanchen No. 98, a Chinese constable, if he went with the Russian constable on the evening of the 6th, he replied that they were in front and he was behind. Asked how Liu Mingshan fell into the river, he replied that he was behind and the Russian constable was in front, more than twenty steps apart. Gu Hongsheng testified that he was 23 years old, from Wuxi, worked as a lacquerer, and lived at No. 4, Alley 223, opposite Little World, and worked with the deceased. Yang Akun testified that he was 21 years old, from Changzhou, worked as a lacquerer, and lived with Gu.

Female Corpse in Shanghai Suitcase, Clues Already Found in Shanghai 159

Transported from the Wanguo Apartment on Avenue Joffre

The transporting car was hired by a Russian

The body examined in Kobe seems to be a Chinese woman

Some say it may be related to a missing Russian woman

The Shanghai Maru of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha, which departed from Shanghai for Japan at 3 p.m. on August 5th, discovered a strange odor when unloading luggage in its baggage hold when the ship arrived in Kobe on the 7th. Upon opening it for inspection, it was found to be the corpse of a murdered woman, about twenty-seven or eight years old. However, the body was so decomposed that her nationality could not be identified. The Kobe Marine Police immediately telegraphed the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai to investigate the person who packed the suitcase. The police department of the Consulate and the police departments of the British and French concessions have all mobilized to investigate. It is reported that the investigation of this case has yielded clues, and the situation will be recorded as follows.

Mobilized Together 160

When the Japanese Consulate-General in this city

received this information, it noted that

a Japanese woman from No. 608 Yuyuan Road

had recently gone missing, so they paid special attention to this. In addition to ordering the police department attached to the consulate to start an investigation, they also notified the public concession and the French concession police authorities separately. Two weeks ago, the French concession authorities reported that a Polish Russian woman, 14 years of age, had gone missing, so they believed that this case might be related. Therefore, they also unanimously mobilized and conducted a close investigation separately.

Investigating the Origin 161

At the same time, the Nippon Yusen Kaisha thought

the suitcase was handled

and reported by the Hongkou Japanese Shanghai Travel Agency.

Now that this bizarre case has occurred, it has also begun to investigate the origin. The company reported that a Western-dressed man contacted the company at the time, but the man's address was not known in detail. So they went to Huishan Wharf, summoned all the workers, and asked who had taken care of this luggage and which company had hired the car. Fortunately, one of the workers remembered that the luggage was transported by the Shanghai Public Transportation Company in this city. Therefore, the company believed that it had obtained some clues and reported everything to all relevant parties.

Police Interrogation 162

After receiving the report, the public concession police

immediately investigated and found that the Public

Transportation Company was located

opposite Avenue Edward VII on North Henan Road. They immediately summoned Chen Gencai, the owner of the company. According to Chen Gencai's report, the car was driven by carter Zhu Aying. So they summoned Zhu Aying, who reported that he was hired by a Russian nicknamed "Little Luo Song" on the noon of August 5th. The Russian was an employee of a certain American transportation department on Renmei Road and was familiar with him. The police then summoned the Russian, who also reported all the details of what happened. However, the above-mentioned people were absolutely irrelevant to the content of this case.

Carter's Report 163

According to carter Zhu Aying,

he was looking for business around

the New Customs Wharf. The Russian, Little

Luo Song, was familiar with him and would always

hire his car to transport goods. At 11:30 a.m. on August 5th, he had just found a job and was planning to go to Yuyuan Road when he met Little Luo Song, who was anxious to transport several pieces of luggage. So, after

first going to Yuyuan Road, he drove to the destination designated by Little Luo Song. When he arrived, there were already many workers who had moved the luggage to the lower ground floor.

Transportation Circumstances 164

There were a total of seven pieces of luggage.

Originally on the second floor, when the car

arrived, they were all moved down.

There were six leather trunks and one iron box. However, the weight of the seven pieces of luggage was extremely heavy. When they were being loaded onto the car, the most noticeable thing was that the contents of the iron box seemed to be moving, and there was a feeling of shaking in the middle. The workers were unable to handle the weight, so they asked another strong worker to help carry it up. After loading everything, they drove to Huishan Wharf. Along the way, Little Luo Song and another unnamed Russian escorted the luggage. When they arrived at the wharf, it was only thirty or forty minutes before the ship was scheduled to depart, so it was immediately hoisted onto the ship and loaded into the baggage hold without being inspected by customs officers. Little Luo Song and others left after the luggage was on the ship. That was all the workers knew.

Corps Found 165

According to a follow-up telegram

from Japan yesterday, the murdered

woman's body has been

examined by a doctor and is confirmed

to be a Chinese woman, about twenty-seven or eight years old, short and very fat, with bound feet and pierced earlobes, and had never given birth. The cause of death was strangulation. There was a wound under her nose, indicating that she had struggled during the murder. According to the autopsy results of Dr. Torelian Mizu of the Hyogo Prefectural Criminal Division, the woman's body appeared to have been beaten to death with a blunt object and it was determined that she was a Chinese woman.

General Guess 166

Currently, all police agencies

and the Japanese Consulate in this city

have gained some clues

about the case, but are still actively investigating. It is said that the luggage was shipped to Nagasaki on the day it was transported, and a Russian went with it. However, the Japanese investigation revealed that the Russian was not involved. As for the woman's clothes, it is said that they were made of Chinese materials, and her ears were pierced, as if she had worn earrings, and her feet had been bound, so it was concluded that she was a Chinese woman. However, since the escort was Russian, it seemed that she was not a Chinese woman. Therefore, the truth is still unknown.

The tragic death of the Chinese beauty in the suitcase

on the Shanghai Maru is being investigated jointly

by the Hyogo Prefectural Criminal Division and the Marine Police. Judging from the writing on the suitcase, the perpetrator is certainly a well-educated person. Worker Acts as Inside Man in Shin Xin No. 6 Factory Robbery Case 168

Stolen factory entry permit to sneak in

Cai and Fan, the two thieves, each sentenced to seven years

On the afternoon of June 15th, at around 8 p.m., the Shin Xin No. 6 Cotton Mill at No. 22 Xihu Road was robbed of wages totaling 2,263 yuan. Subsequently, Fei Kelun, a Chinese detective from the Jiaxing Road police station, arrested the perpetrators Cai Defu, Fan Xiaobing (also known as Li Xiaobing, a coppersmith at the factory), and Gao Deqin. The Shandong woman, Ma Zhangshi (resident of No. 10 Yanshan Road), was also suspected and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefei presided over the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that Fan Xiaobing instigated the case, inviting Cai Defu and Ma Er (the son of Ma Zhangshi), who was at large, to conspire with Gao Deqin and others at Ma Zhangshi's house more than five times. Cai and Ma were smuggled in by Fan Xiaobing using a stolen factory entry permit to carry out the robbery. Although Gao Deqin did not go, he received two yuan of the loot, which he admitted to at the police station, etc. Cai Defu confessed that Fan Xiaobing and Ma Er were responsible for the robbery, and that Ma Er carried the pistol, etc. Fan Xiaobing confessed that a worker surnamed Liao came up with the idea and forced him to join by threatening him with a pistol. At the time of the incident, he had already finished work and was on the lookout near the Huade Road Bridge. After the incident, Ma Er and a person surnamed Ding took the loot, and he did not receive any of it, etc. His confession was evasive. Gao Deqin confessed that he knew Cai Defu, and although he knew the result of the third conspiracy to rob, he did not go. Afterward, Cai Defu gave him two yuan, etc. Ma Zhangshi confessed that Zhang Er was her second son, and he used to wander outside and did not support his elderly mother. Now, he relies on his eldest son, Ma Dadu, to make a living. She knew nothing about the robbery of the yarn factory and begged for leniency. Judge Xiao asked both lawyers to debate the case and then sentenced Cai Defu and Fan Xiaobing to seven years of imprisonment each. Gao Deqin was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. The number of days detained before the judgment was confirmed would be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. Ma Zhangshi was found not guilty. The police lawyer Zhang abandoned the appeal, and she was released in court.

Large Gambling Den Raided in Huile Lane 169

In addition to gambling equipment, there were also smoking paraphernalia

Each defendant was sentenced and fined accordingly

Zhang Wenjun, the Chinese Deputy Head of the Old Zha Police Station, and Bao Tan Wang Jiaju, discovered that someone was organizing the Hexinghao gambling den inside No. 24 Huile Lane on Fuzhou Road, gathering crowds to gamble, skimming profits, and mixing men and women. The stakes were quite high. Therefore, they reported to the Special Court and obtained a search warrant. At around 10 p.m. the night before, they cooperated with West Head Constable Permi to go to the address and arrest the boss Zhu Aqiu, as well as tea server Zhu Asan, Lin Yudi, cook Yang Baosheng, and sixteen gamblers, including Fang Xuezhang, manager of a certain customs brokerage firm, Fang Zhu, Tang Zhu, Chen Li, Tao Baochu, Ma Baishou, Yu Qingsheng, Hu Yongqing, Liu Guihua, Jin Fusheng, Zhang Zilin, and Lin Kaiwu. They confiscated seven dice cups, four sets of mahjong tiles, two sets of wachahua cards, two sets of pai gow tiles, two boxes of chips, 249 yuan in banknotes, one hundred double-cent coins, 106 copper coins, one passbook each from Siming Bank and Wing On Bank, four checkbooks, as well as ledgers, automobile pick-up tickets, and other items. There were also two opium pipes, two opium lamps, five bowls, and fourteen taels of opium paste, which were all taken to the police station. The gamblers were allowed to post a bail of 100 yuan each, and the rest were detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The defendant Zhu Aqiu hired three lawyers, Fan Gang, Wang Peiyuan, and Liu Gui. Yu Qingsheng, who was released on bail, hired lawyer Yu Hualong to appear in court on his behalf. Police lawyer Jiang Baolian stood up and stated the case, saying that the police had confiscated many gambling tools and gambling ledgers as evidence. In addition to prosecuting the first defendant, Zhu Aqiu, for the crime of running a gambling den, he was also charged with illegal possession of smoking paraphernalia under Article 3 of the Prohibition of Opium Act and should be punished according to the law. After Judge Zhan Liangce questioned each defendant one by one and clarified the situation, he sentenced Zhu Aqiu to two months of imprisonment and a fine of 70 yuan. Zhu Asan, Lin Yudi, Yang Baosheng, Liu Guihua, and Jin Fusheng were found not guilty. The remaining ten people, including Fang Xuezhang, were each fined 40 yuan. All confiscated items were confiscated. Zhu Aqiu was allowed to post a bail of 300 yuan pending an appeal and was released to await instructions.

Young Man Jumps into the River and is Rescued 170

At 2:45 p.m. yesterday, the Longmaozhan ferry from Pudong Lujiazui was carrying passengers back to Pudong from the Guangdong Road wharf on the other side when, just as it reached the center of the river, a young man among the passengers suddenly leaped into the raging waves, intending to commit suicide. Water Pipe Burst, Like a Waterfall 171

Reaching a height of about forty feet

At about 4 p.m. on the afternoon of the 7th, a water pipe suddenly burst on Jungong Road, Wusong Section, in East Shanghai, breaking through the pavement of the road by more than five feet. As a result, the water rushed straight out from the cracked area, reaching a height of about forty feet, crossing the road, and shooting to the tops of trees and into the fields on the other side, like a waterfall. The moment the water pipe burst,

traffic was blocked. A group of villagers passing by had to run barefoot, and rickshaws could not avoid the force and could not cross. Only one or two cars were able to drive through at full speed. Later, after villagers reported it to the nearby police station, they notified the water and electricity company, which immediately sent craftsmen to repair it, but the area had already become a swamp. At the time, a Westerner named A.J. Jones

passed by the scene and took a photo with his camera, submitting it to this newspaper, which is reproduced here for printing.

Melon Vendor and Silk Factory Worker Fight in Violent Drama 175

At 1 p.m. the day before yesterday, melon vendors Zhu Suqin and Xia Shuming from Jiangbei were hawking watermelons inside the Yuanhe Silk Factory at No. 216 Route des Soeurs. The craftsmen upstairs in the silk factory, Li Pinyan, scolded Zhu and others for not shouting so loudly. Zhu and others refused to remain silent, so they quarreled with each other. Li was angered by Zhu and others' words and went downstairs to start a fight. Li was no match for Zhu and Xia and was injured on the spot. Tang Sibao, Gu Songting, Zhang Peiyuan, and Duan Jinyang, coppersmiths who worked upstairs with Li, were indignant and rushed downstairs to help. Seeing the crowd, Zhu took a sharp melon-cutting knife and stabbed Tang Sibao's wrist twice. Because Zhu dared to add a sharp knife and was extremely fierce, the crowd dragged Zhu into the factory, closed the door, and beat him severely. Xia Jinhong, the owner of the pancake stall across from the silk factory, first went to mediate, and then joined the battle. When Zhu was surrounded, someone frantically blew the police whistle. Two Chinese policemen from No. 1269 and No. 2399 nearby heard the sound and rushed to knock open the factory door. They saw that Zhu had been beaten and injured and had fallen to the ground, barely breathing. They immediately arrested all the perpetrators and took them to the Huisi Police Station for detention. Detective Shen Dehui was dispatched to send the injured to Renji Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, Li Pinyan and the other seven people, as well as the murder weapon found on the spot, were escorted to the First Special District Local Court, where they were interrogated by Judge Liu Yugui. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the case, saying that Zhu was now in the hospital and requested a postponement. Judge Liu questioned Li and others and ordered them to be detained pending a deferred trial.

Youth Detaches from Communist Party and Commits Suicide 176

Leaving a Letter of Farewell to Communist Friends

At 9 a.m. yesterday, a young man jumped into the river from the Baidu Bridge outside the Suzhou River Estuary and committed suicide. His body sank and then floated. Alas, I am truly a sinner in this world, one who has not made progress. I still hope you will forgive all my sins. In my dying moments, I shout out the final slogan: Strive! Strive for success, hurrah!"

After Mediation by the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, Shin Xin No. 1 Factory Resolves the Bonus Dispute 177

The bonus is temporarily canceled, and new reward and punishment measures are formulated

The case of the cancellation of the bonus at the Shin Xin Textile No. 1 Factory in Zhoujiaqiao has been unsuccessfully negotiated by party and government agencies many times. The Bureau of Social Affairs summoned the Shin Xin No. 1 Factory and the 7th District Cotton Textile Industry Union again the day before yesterday for a final mediation. Wang Xianqing, director of the Mediation Section of the Third Section, presided over the meeting, and Lu Yinchu, an officer from the Municipal Party Committee, attended. After a long period of persuasion, both parties agreed and signed an agreement to resolve the dispute. The workers' bonus for June will be paid at two days' wages, and the bonus for July will be paid at one day's wages. After that, the payment and settlement will be temporarily suspended. When business recovers, it will be discussed again. The factory will formulate measures for the workers' rewards and punishments and submit them to the主管官署 for approval and implementation.

Su Lao Er's Record of Losing His Daughter 179

Hoping that the Daughter Does Not Fall into Prostitution

Living a Husband and Wife Life

Su Lao Er, residing at No. 17, Jin'an Lane, Jiaotong Road, Zhabei, is now 70 years old. His wife is also in her sixties. They have no children and are lonely. Su usually works as a gatekeeper (commonly known as "kan nongtang"). He has some savings. When he was 54, his wife picked up an abandoned baby (female) at the entrance of the lane. They took her home, hired a wet nurse, and raised her. They named her Aifeng, also known as San Nv. They doted on her, cherishing her like a treasure. Aifeng is now 17 years old, quite beautiful. When dressing up, she often goes out to play. Because Su loves her so much, he is relatively lenient in discipline, hoping to find a son-in-law in the future to enjoy his old age. Unexpectedly, Aifeng was incited by scoundrels. A few days ago, she took away clothes and ornaments worth hundreds of yuan, as well as cash, and ran away without a trace. The old couple searched everywhere but could not find her. They were extremely frustrated, deeply afraid that their daughter had fallen into the hands of bandits and would suffer in the future. They specially filed a petition with the court yesterday, stating that if Aifeng does not fall into prostitution in the future and lives a husband and wife life with a good man, they will not pursue the matter. Otherwise, they will sue to the court.

Bamboo Industry Colleagues Unify Water Transport Fees 180

The Bamboo Industry Association of this city held a temporary executive committee meeting yesterday to unify rafting water transport fees. The following resolutions were made: (1) Regarding the proposal to uniformly regulate water transport fees for rafting among colleagues, it was resolved and passed that the rate for Mao bamboo be 7 jiao per tie for flowing head and 8 jiao per tie for square towing (including 3 fen of rafting fee, deducting 5 fen per tie for delivery in Nanshi); the rate for Li bamboo is 4 fen per piece; the rate for Mao wood is 15% higher than the original cost; the rate for Taiwan bamboo towels is 70% off the Mao bamboo price; the rate for Nanshan Mao bamboo is 4 jiao 5 fen per tie (including 5 fen per tie for delivery in Nanshi, including 1 fen 5 li per tie of rafting fee). The above prices will be implemented from August 1st. (2) Regarding how to regulate water transport fees for loading ships among colleagues, it was resolved that the rate for putting Li bamboo into the water is 6 fen per piece, the rate for the Li bamboo in the yard is 5 fen per piece, and the rate for miscellaneous Li goods is 1 jiao per piece. The above is for Xiaoshe, Heping, and Meixi goods. (3) Regarding the proposal that the association is responsible for the rafting land rent in Pudong and the expenses in the Huangpu River, it was resolved to convene each raft household to come to the meeting to talk on the 16th of this month.

The Four Banks' Reserve Warehouse Issues a Preparation Report - No. 188 183

The Four Banks' Reserve Warehouse is jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks. It specializes in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the issuance regulations of the warehouse, the banknotes are fully prepared. The cash reserve is at least 60%, and the guarantee reserve is at most 40%. It is announced once a week, checked by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. Now, according to the 188th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Warehouse on August 5, 1933, the amount of banknotes in circulation is 19,261,137 yuan, and the total amount of reserves is 19,261,137 yuan, including cash reserves of 15,522,037 yuan and guarantee reserves of 3,739,100 yuan.

Zhejiang Industrial Bank Inspection Report 184

The Zhejiang Industrial Bank's 38th inspection report on issuance reserves states that the Zhejiang Industrial Bank's issuance is completely separated from business operations, and the reserves are fully prepared. On the 8th of this month, accountant Yan Ouke inspected and found that the cash reserves were above 60% and the guarantee reserves were below 40%. All the numbers are as follows: the number of banknotes issued by the bank is 4,096,916.5 yuan; the reserves include 2,800,8916.5 yuan in cash and 1,288,000 yuan in guarantees; the amount used by fellow banks is 3,100,000 yuan; the reserves include 1,891,000 yuan in cash and 1,209,000 yuan in guarantees.

"The Wedding Night" Not Published by Women's Bookstore 185

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the "Wedding Night" published by the Women's Bookstore was interfered with by the Municipal Education Bureau because the author falsely used the name of Wuben Girls' School. It is now learned that this book was actually published by Haoyundao Bookstore, falsely using the name of the Women's Bookstore. Yesterday, Ms. Huang Xinmian of the Women's Bookstore heard about this and was filled with indignation. She has hired a lawyer to sue Haoyundao Bookstore for the crime of falsely using her name for profit in accordance with the law.

Weather Report 190

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 pm yesterday said that the coastal areas of Shandong and the Yangtze River basin are hot and cloudy, with no fixed wind direction. There is a gentle east wind along the coast south of Ma'an Island. There are thunderstorms in the afternoon. The center of the typhoon entered within 60 miles of the intersection of 20 degrees north latitude and 113 degrees east longitude at 6 am this morning and blew westward. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 pm yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 94.3 and the lowest was 76.6. On the same day last year, the highest was 93.9 and the lowest was 77.7.

Special Item

Draft of the Municipal Social Bureau's Rural Revival Plan 192

Focus on Stabilizing Farmers' Lives

Regulating Finance and Improving Operations

Is a Pressing Need of the Moment

The Social Bureau issued a draft of the Shanghai Municipal Rural Revival Plan yesterday, saying that in recent years, the agricultural situation in our country has gradually declined, the amount of agricultural crops has been decreasing day by day, the countryside has collapsed, and the economy has gone bankrupt. In order to seek relief, the government has held food conferences, agricultural finance conferences, and silk relief conferences. Recently, the Executive Yuan has organized the Rural Revival Committee to discuss everything in order to plan the revival of the countryside. It has recently issued a general order to all provinces and cities to set up branches of the Rural Revival Committee to assist the central government in all its work. This is an important policy and cannot be delayed. Although Shanghai is a gathering area for industry and commerce, it has more than 500,000 mu of farmland, with villages and dense population. Before the January 28 Shanghai War, farmers, due to the upward trend of living standards and the pressure of the urban economy, found it difficult to maintain the livelihood of a family with the output of farmland. They often came to Shanghai to work in factories during slack farming seasons and still went home to cultivate during busy farming seasons. The rural economy can be greatly adjusted. Since the January 28 War, not only the villages in Zhabei have been repeatedly looted and burned, and their family property has been destroyed. The rural areas in other districts have also suffered extremely heavy economic blows. Moreover, after the war, various factories, due to economic pressure, either announced the suspension of business or implemented wage cuts. Farmers in this city who usually use the slack farming season to work in factories have no place to set foot. The economic income of farming families has been greatly reduced. The crisis of rural bankruptcy is imminent. When the Executive Yuan orders this city to organize a branch of the Rural Revival Committee, I will put forward the plan to revive the rural areas of this city based on what I have seen, hoping to adopt it. Reviving the countryside is useless to the actual situation to talk empty words. It is necessary to raise considerable funds and proceed in stages to be effective. Now that the rural areas of this city are on the verge of bankruptcy, if we want to revive it, we cannot achieve it overnight. We must first conduct a detailed investigation, find out the causes of rural decline, and then find ways to help, prescribe medicine according to the symptoms, so that farmers can return to normal, have enough food and clothing, live and work in peace, so that they can engage in rural revitalization and various constructions. Therefore, to revive the countryside, we must first provide considerable relief, otherwise, if we do not improve its foundation and work on its end, we have not seen that it can be effective. If farmers have no time to save themselves from death, how can they encourage their remaining courage to seek revival and construction? Therefore, before discussing rural revival, we should first discuss rural relief, which is described as follows:

First Relief Methods

As mentioned earlier, to revive the countryside, the first thing is to relieve the farmers, so that they can live and work in peace, and do not change their minds, leave the countryside, and flee to the cities, which is the most important plan. Those who engage in agriculture are farmers. If we do not first maintain their lives and stabilize them, and desire them to improve agriculture and develop the economy with a body that is hard-working all day long but cannot be full, it is like climbing a tree to catch fish. The relief measures are described as follows: (to be continued)

Educational Film Association Seeks to Improve Foreign Films 193

The Chinese Educational Film Association believes that many foreign films coming to China do not conform to our national conditions. If we only take passive inspection and banning, it is not a thorough solution. Therefore, the five educational film material selection standards set by the association, and examples to prove what kind of films are welcomed by our country, have been translated into English. The association has sent them to European and American film companies as a reference for future film production, in order to correct foreigners' psychology and seek sincere cooperation with each other. The translated English letters have been sent to the executive and supervisory committees of the association for safekeeping.

Zhejiang Provincial Experimental Agricultural School Completed 195

Lan Mengjiu Appointed President

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education has newly established an experimental agricultural school. The location has been designated as Tangya, Jinhua. New students will be recruited soon. The preparation director of the school, who has been hired as the president, is Lan Mengjiu, the current professor of the Agricultural College of Peking University. Mr. Lan is an educator who is both theoretical and practical. It is not easy to complete the preparation in the shortest time. The school was originally planned by Director Chen Bulei and Wu Juenong. Later, due to busy work, Lan was specially appointed to be responsible for the implementation. The outline of the school organization and curriculum is practical and local, which opens up a new way for domestic agricultural education. In addition, the teachers recently hired by the school are all experts in China who are knowledgeable and thoughtful and can work hard.

Municipal Education Bureau Carefully Selects and Appoints Elementary School Teachers 199

(Central News Agency) In the past, the municipal elementary school teachers in this city were appointed by the principals and reported to the Bureau of Education for record. This semester, the Bureau of Education followed the regulations for elementary schools promulgated by the Ministry and revised the rules for the appointment and dismissal of municipal elementary school teachers. It ordered all schools to appoint teachers in accordance with the selection of qualified personnel to be reported to the Bureau for approval before hiring them, in order to emphasize the importance of teachers. Recently, elementary schools have submitted the list of teachers they intend to hire, filling out the appointment forms and submitting the registration certificates to the Bureau for review. Occasionally, one or two principals, in order to show favor to others, also list unqualified personnel in the forms to try their luck. It is said that the Bureau of Education will severely reprimand them to serve as a warning.

After the Prohibition of "The Wedding Night" 200

Statement from the Women's Bookstore

Yesterday, we received a letter from Huang Xinmian of the Women's Bookstore, which stated: "To the respected Mr. Reporter, yesterday, your newspaper published an article entitled 'Author of 'The Wedding Night' Impersonates Wu Ben' (Editor's note: This article was sent by the Shanghai News Agency for publication). The content involves our bookstore. After reading it, our colleagues were filled with indignation. They immediately went to Haoyundao Bookstore on Jiaotong Road and purchased a copy of the book. On the copyright page, it indeed stated 'Published by Shanghai Women's Bookstore.' Upon investigation, our bookstore has always aimed to assist women's education and develop women's knowledge and never publishes vulgar books. This book was clearly published by Haoyundao Bookstore, and the owner of the book is the owner of the bookstore. They dare to disregard the law and steal the name of our bookstore, which is extremely hateful. The Municipal Bureau of Education did not investigate with our bookstore first but announced it in the newspaper, which is also too rash. In addition to filing a lawsuit according to the law, our bookstore has always admired your newspaper's reliable record of history. Therefore, we dare to present the facts and responsibly send this letter requesting a correction to avoid confusing the public. Please accept our greetings, August 8th."

New Development of Southeast Women's Physical Education Teachers' College 204

Purchase of more than ten acres of land to build a swimming pool and campus

Since its establishment, Southeast Women's Physical Education Teachers' College in Jiangwan has taken a pragmatic approach as its purpose. Over the past nine years, its equipment has been complete, its courses have been serious, and its talents have emerged. The graduates of each class have served at home and abroad, and many of them have been trusted by people from all walks of life. The school had previously built a new school building on Xiangyin Road in Jiangwan in 1931 of the Republic of China because the number of students coming to study was increasing. The physical education facilities, such as the gymnasium, the track and field, and various outdoor ball fields, were fully equipped. It is said that Principal Yu believes that the promotion of women's swimming in our country is essential, so he had the motive of building a swimming pool early on, but it was interrupted by the Shanghai Incident. Now, he is still proceeding with the realization of the swimming pool with his original intention of running the school. With the support of parents last month, he purchased more than ten acres of land near the school yesterday to build a large-scale swimming pool and a quiet campus. He is now planning everything and will start construction soon.

In addition, the elementary school department has also added graduates of the school's normal department, Ms. Zheng Senlan, Ms. Li Biyun, Ms. Yang Xianzhu, and Ms. Yu Huiying.

New Plans for New Huan School 206

Since New Huan Elementary School moved to the new school building at the intersection of Parker Road and Kuling Road and added a junior commercial vocational school, on the one hand, it has been supported by the school board members Chu Minyi, Wu Xingya, Du Yuesheng, Wang Boqun, Lin Kanghou, Liu Zainen, Jiang Wenyu, Zheng Tonghe, Wang Xiaoying, Pan Yangyao, Shen Yizhen, Lu Shaoji, He Yangxian, Wu Ruinian, and Zhou Zanming. On the other hand, with the planning and management of school affairs by principals Zhang Zhonghuan and Zhang Xinbo, it is progressing rapidly. Faculty and staff have been hired. Vocational school teachers are all experts who graduated from famous universities. Elementary school teachers are mostly graduates of the normal schools of the provincial Shangzhong and municipal Wuben schools. The equipment is all new and pays attention to hygiene. In addition to Principal Zhang donating thousands of private collections of books to the school, a large number of books, instruments, typewriters, pianos, etc. have been continuously added. For the sake of student practice, a consumer cooperative has been set up first, and practice banks will be added in the future. At the same time, in order to reduce the burden on parents, the school tuition is extremely low and scholarships and free students are provided. It is said that in order to meet social needs, the school has an affiliated night school and women's remedial school, and there has been a very enthusiastic response recently. The school is currently trying to rent several school buildings nearby to develop.

The National Games Will Not Be Postponed 208

The Ninth Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games Organizing Committee Decides

The Far Eastern Preliminary Competition Next Year Will No Longer Be Held

The Conference Will Be Held Continuously for Ten Days Starting on National Day

The Completion of the Venue Renovation Project, etc. is Limited in Time

Measures are Planned for Traffic and Security at the Venue

(Nanjing, 8th dispatch) The National Games Organizing Committee resolved eight major cases at the ninth standing committee meeting on the evening of the 7th.

Eight Important Resolutions of the Standing Committee 209

(1) The National Games will not be postponed. (2) There is no need to add inscriptions to the existing prizes and trophies, and supplements will be made according to the number to be awarded this year. Director Xu et al. will draft a concrete plan for discussion at the next meeting. (3) Designate a location so that the Telegraph Bureau can set up a telegraph office and hang lines at the venue. (4) Reviewed and approved the Security Group's revised work plan, budget and organizational chart. (5) The renovation of venues, dormitories, and water supply projects must be completed before the middle of September, and Guan Songsheng will be hired as an engineering consultant. (6) A letter will be sent to the Police Department requesting additional police officers to maintain order at all stations from Xiaguan to the Central Stadium. (7) Please ask the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to install road signs. (8) Recommend Wu Yunrui to serve concurrently as the venue equipment director, and Wu Bangwei will continue to serve as the registration and allocation director.

Selection of Far Eastern Representatives Simultaneously 210

Regarding the selection of athletes to represent our country at the 10th Far Eastern Games, it was decided to select them at this National Games. Because the period between the two games is only half a year, active practice during the transition period can gradually improve technology. The training methods before participation and the standards for determining athletes must be discussed and decided by the Organizing Committee in detail.

The Conference Will Be Held Continuously for Ten Days 211

The duration of this National Games is scheduled to be held continuously for ten days from October 10th. However, in the event of insufficient time for ball games or special circumstances, it may be extended temporarily by the Committee.

Swimming Pool Planned to Be Borrowed from Military School 212

Regarding the construction of the venue, it has already begun around the venue. It is planned to divide the area and build sheds to set up temporary shops. Regarding the swimming problems of the conference, the original swimming pool of the Central Stadium, on the one hand, has not been filled with water after it was built, nor has it been covered. Cracks have appeared at the bottom, and there is a risk of leakage. If it cannot be applied at that time, it is planned to borrow the swimming pool of the Central Military Academy to be prudent.

(Nanjing Communication) The 22nd National Games have been scheduled to be held in Nanjing on October 10th. The venue of the conference was assigned on the first of this month to receive members from the Mausoleum Management Committee. It is now engaged in the layout of the venue. There have been claims that the Far Eastern Games are scheduled to be held, and it would be best to reschedule this year's Games to the spring of next year as a preliminary selection for the Far Eastern Games. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency stationed in Beijing recently visited the authorities in charge of the National Games to inquire about the opinions on the rescheduling issue and the preparations for the athletes' congress and ticket sales to participate in the Far Eastern Games. The reply is as follows:

No Rescheduling 213

According to the discussion, it is said that the conference must be rescheduled to be held in the spring of next year. This claim is purely a personal opinion, because the decision of this National Games to be held on October 10th is due to: (1) This National Games is a continuation of the 20th National Games and is held on National Day according to previous resolutions. (2) Autumn is better than spring for weather. Summer and winter are not suitable for sports, and there is a lot of rain in spring. It is not possible to stop the Games halfway, and sports are also quite inconvenient. Due to the weather, autumn is the most suitable for the National Games. (3) Since the preparation of this Association, its important work has been roughly arranged, and it can be opened as scheduled as soon as it is carried out separately. If it is suddenly stopped, not only is time uneconomical, but also the loss of funds is uncountable. For the above reasons, this National Games cannot be rescheduled.

Far Eastern Athletes 214

As for the issue of selecting athletes to attend the next Far Eastern Games, according to regulations, a preliminary competition should be held in the country first. However, at this time when the country's economy is stretched, we are unwilling to engage in waste. In order to save money, it has been decided not to hold a separate preliminary competition. Therefore, the athletes who attend the Far Eastern Games will be determined at this National Games. However, at that time, there are still half a year before the Far Eastern Games. It is planned to set a time after the selection and practice on time. The method for deciding the athletes still needs to be discussed in detail by the Organizing Committee.

Vehicle Distribution 215

The issue of temporary vehicles for the National Games was decided by the 20th National Games Preparatory Committee to borrow 100 cars from various provinces and cities to facilitate the return of athletes and spectators. A temporary station was set up to specially pick up and send athletes and spectators. In order to save money, this year it was reduced to fifty vehicles. It is learned that the Organizing Committee said that the 50 cars still need a lot of gasoline every day. Therefore, it is planned to use the prepared vehicles to pick up and send athletes and conference staff only. Spectators are generally on their own to save vehicles and save public funds. Regarding the construction of temporary stations, it is estimated that more than 2,000 yuan will be needed. We have contacted large car dealers in Shanghai and are preparing to negotiate exchange conditions on the principle of no cost. Otherwise, a temporary tarpaulin station will be built.

Ticket Sales at the Venue 216

The sale of tickets to the audience at the venue was originally set at 10 cents per ticket according to the decision of the 20th Organizing Committee. This year, in order to make up for the expenses, it will be changed to 20 cents. However, according to the opinions of the general organizing committee, it is believed that in order to promote sports, the ticket price cannot be raised, increasing the burden on the people and reducing the enthusiasm of the audience. According to the budget of the Association, the income from ticket sales is about 27,000 yuan, while the temporary expenses at the venue are at least more than 35,000 yuan. Therefore, the income and expenditure at the venue are still insufficient by more than 8,000 yuan. The temporary remedy is to post advertisements on the day of the National Games. At the same time, the area around the venue is divided into temporary shop areas, so that shops can be set up in the venue, and the audience can buy snacks at any time and collect rent to make up for the temporary expenses of the venue.

Conference Period of Ten Days 217

The duration of the conference is scheduled to be ten days from October 10th to October 20th. If there is not enough time for ball games, the Conference Committee may decide to extend the date. Regarding the National Arts, the General Assembly originally had regulations for National Arts competitions. However, this year, the Central National Arts Museum plans to take advantage of this time and place to hold the National Arts National Examination. It is learned that the site of the National Arts martial arts competition is very small and cannot accommodate a large number of people. Therefore, if the National Arts National Examination is held at the same time as the National Games, a separate location must be found, otherwise it must be held after the closing of the conference. This has not yet been determined.

Good Food and Accommodation 218

The Preparatory Committee is paying close attention to the issue of the meals for the athletes during the conference. It is planned to build a large reed shed next to the venue and recruit chefs from Jiangsu, Anhui, Guangdong, Sichuan, Ping, and Shaanxi, and other places to choose and eat by category. The conference is not responsible for it, which can save money and is convenient. Under the stands of the conference venue, in addition to some offices, the rest are dormitories for athletes. Two rows of wooden beds are set up in a room, divided into left and right rows. The bed is made of three layers. A room can accommodate twenty-four people. Statistics show that the dormitory area of the entire venue is sufficient for 2,000 people. In the corridor around the room, you can only see rows of room doors, which are neat and impressive. As for the conference staff, it is planned to use the school building of the Orphans' School in Zhongshanmen as a place to stay.

Zheng Zhaojia and Wang Wenzheng to Finalize the Chinese Open Tennis Singles Today 222

Held at the Chinese Tennis Court at 4 pm

Zheng Zhaojia Won Ma Anquan in Straight Sets Yesterday

The Chinese Open Tennis Singles Competition has reached the finals week since the start of the game. Zheng Zhaojia and Wang Wenzheng are scheduled to play in the final at the Chinese Tennis Court at 4 pm today to determine who will win the championship. In yesterday's semi-final between Zheng Zhaojia and Ma Anquan, Zheng won Ma 6-3, 6-2, 6-2. Today's final between Zheng and Wang is the first most exciting competition since Shanghai Chinese has a formal singles championship competition. (Note: Qiu Feihai and Lin Baohua did not participate in the Chinese Singles Championship, so the competition interest has not been strong over the years. The Zheng Wang battle this year is the most exciting, enough to compare with Lin Baohua and Qiu Feihai)

Yesterday's Semi-Final 223

Yesterday, the semi-final between Zheng Zhaojia and Ma Anquan, Zheng won in straight sets quite easily. A brief account of the process is as follows:

▲First Set: After the start, Zheng used low, fast shots to attack fiercely, making it difficult for Ma Anquan to parry, losing three games in a row. Ma then rallied himself, winning back two games, then made it four to three. Zheng won with six to three.

▲Second Set: Both won one game at the start. Zheng then added three games in a row, making it four to one, and then each added one game, winning six to two. In this set, Zheng repeatedly went to the net, with alternating gains and losses.

▲Third Set: Zheng's shots became more and more powerful, making it difficult for Ma Anquan to parry. Zheng won four games in a row. In the next game, Zheng lost one game due to self-destruction. Afterwards, each added one game, and Zheng finally won again with six to two.

Today's Final 224

▲Past Records: In this competition, Zheng Zhaojia had a bye in the preliminary round. In the second round, he won against Mao Hongfa with six to two, six to two, and nine to seven. In the semi-final, he won against Li Nan with three to six, six to two, six to two, and six to three. In the semi-final, he won against Ma Anquan with six to three, six to two, and six to two. Wang Wenzheng also had a bye in the preliminary round. In the second round, his opponent Zheng Zirong retired due to an arm injury. In the semi-final, he won against Sun Linfang with three to six, six to one, six to three, and six to one. In the semi-final, he won against Yu Tianguang with six to three, six to four, and six to zero. Looking at the two's records, they appear to be quite even.

▲Qualifications of the Two: Wang Wenzheng's background is similar to that of the famous French tennis player Cochet. From a young age, he served as a ball boy on the tennis court. From picking up balls, he progressed to become a Marker. He has been living on the tennis court for about twenty years. Having seen and heard so much, and through his own practice, his experience is the most extensive and his qualifications are the oldest in the country. This year, he regained his amateur status and is participating in a formal championship competition for the first time. He has great hopes. His skill is comparable to that of Qiu Feihai, but his connections are not as good as Qiu. As for Zheng Zhaojia, he is an outstanding talent in the youth circle of our country. Although his experience and qualifications are not as good as Wang Wenzheng, his skills have surpassed his predecessors. He has attended important championship competitions many times and is comparable to Lin Qiu.

▲Final Situation: Wang is known for his skillful play and few self-inflicted errors, while Zheng is known for his power and connections. Today's final will be as grand as the Qiu-Lin battle in the past. The audience's comments are divided, with some saying that Zheng Zhaojia can win and others saying that Wang Wenzheng can win. Because of this, the tennis community has great interest and hope in this final. It is enough to show the emerging atmosphere of the tennis community. In today's battle, it is hoped that the two will show their inherent strengths and give a very wonderful performance to reward the audience. Then victory is certainly gratifying, and defeat is also honorable.
