Essays

A Farewell Gift to This Year's Students Studying Abroad 228

— Jun Ti

The time for studying abroad comes around again. We hold endless hopes for the students studying abroad. As they are about to leave their motherland and go to foreign countries to seek the latest science and revive China, I cannot help but learn from the ancients and write a few parting words. Whether they listen or not is up to them, whether I write or not is up to me. In the Han Dynasty of our country, only foreigners came to China to study. It was not until the Tang Dynasty that people went abroad to study. Everyone knows that it was the Tang Monk Chen Xuanzang who went to the Western Paradise to obtain Buddhist scriptures. In an era of inconvenient transportation, he did not fear the dangers of mountains and rivers and went to India to study Buddhist scriptures. After returning to the country, he and his disciples translated 75 Buddhist scriptures. The highest philosophy of Buddhism was introduced to China by him, and the original philosophy of China was greatly influenced. This is the first success!

The second one is Xu Guangqi from Shanghai in the late Ming Dynasty. Although he never went abroad, he studied astronomy from foreigners, which is the same as the purpose of studying abroad. His teacher was the Italian Mr. Li Maibao, who was wearing the official uniform of the Ming Dynasty and hung in the Catholic Church. In addition to astronomy, he also studied firearms. He translated many books. Chinese people who studied Western academics probably started with Mr. Xu. I have seen a Shanghai gazetteer in English with a portrait of him, wearing the official uniform of the Ming Dynasty (not wearing a suit), standing upright in the center, with a globe and his works on the table next to him. This kind of spirit is beyond reach. This is the second success!

The third one is Yan Fu from Minhou in the late Qing Dynasty, a student studying in the United Kingdom. He translated many books, with Yuanfu, Tianyanlun, and Mueller's Mingxue being the most famous. Unfortunately, he was full of knowledge, but the Qing court could not reuse him. Being granted the title of Jinshi was the end of his study abroad career. It can be seen that his classmate, Ito Hirobumi of Japan, transformed Japan so that it was changing with each passing day. But although he did not get a position in politics! In the academic world, it is a different color. It can also be regarded as the third success!

The above three people, after completing their studies, the books they wrote were translations. They did not use the original text to teach people, but translated the original text into Chinese to teach people. From this, we can know the right and wrong of using the original text and the native language. Of course, I dare not say that the current students studying abroad do not have the knowledge of the three of them; nor dare I say that the current students studying abroad do not have the works of the three of them. But taking the number of students studying abroad in the past few decades as a ratio, the talents produced are too few to satisfy our hopes! It is also embarrassing to say that Japan has been reformed for 50 years, and for every important foreign book, they have a translation; for every new book published abroad, a Japanese translation can be seen within a few months. China has also been reformed for decades, but the textbooks used in universities are in the original text, and the scores are also in the original text. Isn't this treating China as a country without writing? I have also asked several professors, what is the reason? They said: "There are no good textbooks" or "It is more convenient" (convenient for oneself, not convenient for others), and even said "It is impossible to understand without using the original text." This can only be considered as an excuse. However, how to make textbooks with good translations, or original textbooks, and how to make the inconvenient convenient, who should take this responsibility? This is something that I would like to ask the students studying abroad to pay special attention to!

If not, we only need to invite a large number of foreigners to teach, and that's it: why bother to travel across the ocean to sell some raw materials and not be able to turn them into manufactured goods?

A Morning at the Hotel 229

— Yu

The deathly silent hotel

is sleeping in the faint morning light. Last night's singing, shadows, red lights, and green wine: undoubtedly it is already silent, waiting for the coming of night.

In another room, maybe they are still having their good dreams, sweet dreams, hating the ruthlessness of the morning.

Most of the stupid, scheming fame and wealth seekers have already woken up in the middle of the night, but are waiting for the morning of today to implement their pre-planned plan.

The rickshaw pullers waiting at the door do not care about "night" or "morning," only hoping that there will be more passengers than yesterday to maintain their lives.

A morning at the hotel is really a silhouette of the world.

Bonus Year 230

— Quyu

A large bonus is just like the embroidered ball thrown by the princess to recruit a son-in-law in the old novels. It spins down in the air and lands on the lucky person. A thunderclap on the ground means getting a beautiful wife; becoming a son-in-law; wealth and glory, everything is complete. If a person wins a bonus, the amount is small, they can change seasons; go to the dance hall, and enjoy the present. If the amount is large, a foreign house, a car, and beautiful concubines can all be put to use at once.

"Read, read, read! There are golden houses in books. Read, read, read! There are Yan Ruyu and a thousand Zhong of millet in books." These words are really out of date in this 20th century modern era. If you read books, you are sure to starve to death and have no hope of getting rich. Only by buying lottery tickets can you have the blessing of your ancestors; the god of luck is following behind you. As soon as the lottery is drawn, it is the first prize, and hundreds of thousands of taels of white money are received. Marry a "Yan Ruyu"; build a "golden house"; happily spend money to move a "thousand Zhong of millet". Wouldn't it be everything you wished for in life? Buy, buy, buy! There are golden houses in the lottery ticket. Buy, buy, buy! There are Yan Ruyu in the lottery ticket. Buy, buy, buy! There are a thousand Zhong of millet in the lottery ticket. To put it more modestly, there are also bonuses for smoking cigarettes. You can choose any brand. The biggest first prize is 5,000 yuan; and the last one is also a cigarette. There are also prizes for drinking beer; there are also prizes for buying patterned cloth; in addition, mosquito incense, soap, buying books, visiting amusement parks: it is simply countless. Shanghai is full of bonuses. Whoever has a bright forehead; whoever has good luck, the spent banknotes: the white dollars, will fly into your pocket.

All kinds of businesses, except coffin shops, hospitals, and human meat markets, have not issued lottery tickets. In addition, there is a possibility of setting up bonuses. If you are not sure, the boss of the coffin shop will be jealous; the hospital and the human meat market will also issue lottery tickets in order to solicit business. The dead will definitely follow one after another; the hospital will hang a full sign; pieces of human flesh will be pressed into dried people, and the groups will come to receive this bonus. This year is the year of national goods. National goods have not been sold well, so it is better to set it as a bonus year. Lottery tickets are flying all over the sky; bonuses are rolling all over the ground. The people of the whole country strive to seize these many bonuses.

Four Northeast Company Commanders 231

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirteen: Abandoning the dark to seek the light, a beauty tacitly agrees

Inheriting the family tradition, strong men have a wild revelry

It was acceptable to accommodate Wang Shili's words and discuss it with a person or two. Even if he did not do it, there was no need to rush in a day or two. This thought of procrastination almost canceled out half of his idea of changing jobs that day. This day passed. The next day at twelve o'clock, the brothers were taking a nap. Zhao Ziqiang had nothing to do, so he walked out of the camp and went to the wilderness to walk around, so that he could think about his worries. Not far from Xiyuan is the Imperial Street leading to Longevity Mountain. Passing through the street, the sound of knives and spoons clattered in the restaurants, followed by bursts of oily aroma, drilling into his nose, causing people's appetite to unknowingly follow the aroma. He reached out and opened the cotton cloth curtain of a restaurant facing the street and walked in. A waiter greeted him with a smile and said, "Company Commander Zhao, what a rare visit! It's been a long time since you've taken care of us." Zhao Ziqiang said with a smile, "I haven't been paid for two months, what am I going to take care of you with? Can I eat things without paying?" The waiter said with a smile, "Company Commander Zhao is really a good person. You were paid today, so you came to take care of us today." Zhao Ziqiang laughed and said, "You really know how to talk. You would be willing to let me eat on credit even if I didn't have money, but you said that I came to eat today because I was paid. I want to ask you, how do you know that I was paid today?" The waiter said with a smile, "There is Company Commander Guan, you know him too, right? He said himself that he would come here for a few drinks whenever he was paid. He came here today, so I thought you must have been paid." Zhao Ziqiang sat down in a seat at the entrance, rubbing his hands together, and said with a smile, "You have seen through us. (Note: This means digging deeper.) We can't eat at small restaurants if we don't get paid?" The waiter did not answer this sentence. Someone in the private room behind him laughed and answered, "This is not wrong at all." As he spoke, the man lifted the curtain and came out. It was Guan Yaowu. Zhao Ziqiang said with a smile, "So you are here drinking. Did you get paid alone?" Guan Yaowu said, "I have been working hard all year round, and I have been living a simple life for a long time. Regardless of whether I am paid or not, I have to be comfortable. Come, come, come! Let's have a few drinks together." As he spoke, he pulled Zhao Ziqiang into the private room. (153)

Enjoying the Cool Breeze 232

— Rongyu

The fire-umbrella-like sun also knows that it is forcing the people too hard, and cleverly hides behind the West Mountain for a while. The people who live in pigeon-cage-like houses, when they see the scorching sun go away, happily wave their fans; wear their slippers, and gather on the streets to enjoy the cool. They relieve their day's stagnation and enjoy the coolness and breeze of the night.

The cement sidewalks; the sides of the alleys are full of men and women sitting on rattan chairs and low stools. Most of the men are bare-chested; their trouser legs are rolled up to their calves. The women are wearing thin gauze shirts, showing their curves; their bare feet and jade legs are displayed very publicly. Who said that China is not promoting nude sports? The place to enjoy the cool is half naked.

The Ningbo woman from the East family is talking loudly about the chaotic dream of riding a white horse last night, and she bet a lot of money on him in the flower club, but a black dog came out. She sighed and said that Zhang Jiu the old monkey was making fun of her. The Suzhou woman is speaking softly about the mahjong sutra, and she has just won a four-fan card with flowers, winning several silver dollars. Young men and women are talking about the layout of the Grand Bright Cinema; the inability of the "White Sisters" film to have a grand reunion is very boring. Many children are squatting on the ground, gesticulating, and lecturing about how the Golden Arhat used a flying sword to cut off the head of the evil tyrant. There are also coolies in blue cloth shirts, recounting how Little Maozi in the nailing shed is so affectionate and righteous. This open-air meeting is really vivid and colorful; a hundred dramas are presented.

Gradually, the night is getting late, and the people who are enjoying the cool are feeling a little tired. A burst of erhu sounds comes from afar; followed by a sharp throat, an unnatural singing voice: "Sister is in that room: the first month is the New Year:"" singing while advertising. The nosy people stopped him and told him to sing. He can also hum a few donkeys and horses Peking opera tunes; he can also sing the new-style drizzle, sister I love you; he can also sing the old-style Four Seasons of Longing, Eighteen Touches. After singing for a while, everyone took out a few copper coins and put them together to give to the artist who dedicated his art to the public. The sound of the erhu and singing gradually faded away: people also felt tired, some lay down in the open air; some went back to the house to fight with bed bugs and resist the heat and stuffiness.

People's Mini-Chronicles

Two Envoys Named Zhang 233

— Zhen

Among the newly appointed seven ambassadors abroad, only two are in the country, and the remaining five are all overseas. Recently, these two have both scheduled to sail to Belgium and Portugal to take up their new posts. The one stationed in Belgium is Zhang Naiyan, the former president of National Central University, and the one stationed in Portugal is Zhang Xinhai, an old professor at National Central University. Saying "old professor" means that his qualifications are old. As early as the Dongda era, he was a professor in the Department of Western Literature. Speaking of age, these two Zhang ambassadors are both under forty years old, so they cannot be considered old. Speaking of appearance, they are both handsome and calm, and full of energy. They are worthy of being the new Chinese ambassadors abroad. There is no old-fashioned style at all. In short, they do not lack any of the characteristics that an ambassador should have in terms of appearance.

Ambassador Zhang stationed in Portugal temporarily acted as a translator for Mei Lanfang when Bernard Shaw came to Shanghai this spring. His eloquence was so impressive that he attracted the attention of people in Shanghai. He has served as a counselor in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for many years, and once served as the acting director of the European and American Department; however, because of his strong personality and difficulty in getting along with others, I wonder if his nature will be changed after traveling far away? He is rarely seen publishing articles in the country; but overseas, especially in various American magazines, his works can often be read. A writer who is well-known abroad is almost unknown in the country; this is very meaningful!

Ambassador Zhang stationed in Belgium originally studied chemistry (Indanthrene blue color cannot be washed away, which he invented); however, since returning to China, he has gained considerable reputation in the writing world by writing "The Complete History of the World War". Then the Commercial Press published the Yunlu Historical Series for him. The writing is beautiful and the material is carefully selected. It is not comparable to crudely made works. Some people say that his appearance is quite similar to Yan Huiqing, but I don't know if Ambassador Yan is also "a harmonious person" who sees people with "a smile on his face? It should be known that this Ambassador Zhang is not offensive to others, unlike that Ambassador Zhang who is difficult to get along with.

Ambassador Zhang stationed in Portugal declared that he would study the complete history of Sino-Portuguese diplomacy, because Portugal has a long history of trade with us, so the history is naturally longer and worth studying in detail. Ambassador Zhang stationed in Belgium, presumably has a background in historical research, so he declared that he would conduct a horizontal investigation of Belgium. Zhang Jingjiang is his uncle, and has already found a way for him to allocate one or two thousand from the Construction Committee for him to use as investigation expenses.

Three Monk-Poets of the Republic of China 234

— Liu Pu

Among monks who are famous for their poetry and have outstanding artistic talent, there are three since the Republic of China: (1) Manshu, (2) Jing'an, and (3) Hongyi.

Manshu's original surname was Su. He was a person with rich "natural wit", produced good poetry and prose, leaving behind grief and sympathy for later generations, which is truly indelible for thousands of years. Especially in recent years, after the praise of Mr. Liu Yazi and Mr. Shou Juan, he has attracted the attention of young people. All those who have been attacked by the waves of the times and are stained with helpless emotions love to read his poetry and prose. Because Manshu's poetry and prose can express the thoughts and feelings that people cannot easily express, and can say the beautiful feelings that people cannot say, but everyone can experience, that is, the so-called "scratching the itch." Therefore, his poignant and lingering, sad and clear verses are often people's best consolation.

Secondly, Jing'an is Master Jichan. He is proficient in internal scriptures and also good at chanting, and has published "The Collection of Eight-Fingered Ascetic." His inner practice is sincere, so his poems and lyrics are also very cold and elegant, without making frivolous words. It is rare to do so, and it is also an exception. I once saw one of his poems: "Layman Vimalakirti is too rampant, where does the heavenly girl come to scatter wonderful fragrance, I laugh at my Zen heart like a dead tree, it doesn't matter if flower branches accompany me." It is more interesting, and it is probably a temporary improvisation? Jing'an passed away in the early years of the Republic of China, when he rushed to the old capital to maintain the temple and petition the authorities. Unexpectedly, he was only in Beijing for less than ten days before he passed away.

As for Master Hongyi, his original surname was Li, and his name was Shutong. He once served as a newspaper editor and school teacher. He was proficient in painting, good at poetry and prose, and famous in the art world. He was also a rare genius in the world. However, in his later years, he abandoned learning and indulged in Zen, entered the empty door, practiced asceticism, and disciplined himself extremely strictly.

Securities and Government Bonds Experience Strong Decline 240

Large Quantities Dumped in the Financial World

Short-Term Financials Drop $1.80 During Trading

Yesterday at the Chinese Securities Exchange, due to the stable situation and the perceived resolution of the crisis, the No. 46 firm in the financial world sold very aggressively, taking advantage of the firming market sentiment. Each item was sold, especially short-term financials. Northern firms, seeing the large influx of goods, did not temporarily cover short positions, as they did not know the full extent of No. 46's selling capacity. Market prices declined sharply due to the congestion of chips. This was a special phenomenon of temporarily disengaging from the environment and had no fundamental relationship to the increase or decrease. The reason is that once the selling stops, the rebound will be very fast. In the morning opening, bonds from the 18th and 19th years, although in a downward trend, only differed by two to three jiao. Starting with the 20th year, various firms, seeing the aggressive selling volume of the No. 46 firm, gave up on buying and watched to take advantage of the situation, and fell more significantly. Salt tax was relatively superior. Only short-term financials fell sharply by $1.80 during one trading session, due to the urgent selling by the No. 46 firm. In the next session, market sentiment softened. Northern firms not only did not cover but took the opportunity to release more, and market prices rebounded even less, ranging from five jiao to seven or eight jiao. When the auction reached salt tax, there were more buyers. This month was only a small decrease of 1.5 jiao, and next month was only a small decrease of 5 fen. Short-term financials, due to the No. 46 firm stopping selling, suddenly saw a rebound of seven or eight jiao. After that, they generally rebounded firmly. As a result, market prices uniformly rebounded by four or five jiao to $1.23. In the future, if the No. 46 firm does not sell off again, it will be very easy for market prices to rebound. The total number of transactions was 13,874,000 yuan, including 4,000 yuan of spot goods. Futures were 4,760,000 for total salt tax, 1,550,000 for troop reduction, 1,460,000 for Ruguan concessions, 2,330,000 for twenty-year concessions, and 1,860,000 for short-term financials. The rest ranged from tens of thousands to hundreds of thousands.

Business Tips (28)

Fine Vermicelli: A Versatile and Inexpensive Ingredient for Meat and Vegetarian Dishes 261

Dried vermicelli is produced in Longkou, Yantai, Jiangbei, and other places. Longkou vermicelli is considered the best quality. It is made from top-grade mung bean flour. The strands are extremely fine, with a clean white color and luster. They are also longer in length and have good tensile strength when dried, making them less likely to break, resulting in very few broken pieces. Yantai vermicelli is second best, made from lower-grade mung bean flour. The strands are coarser and shorter, lacking tensile strength, resulting in more broken pieces. They often clump together in bird's nest shapes. Jiangbei vermicelli is the lowest grade, with a yellow color and even coarser, shorter strands, being brittle and easily broken, and the output is also small. Therefore, Longkou vermicelli is the most popular due to its superior quality. It is a durable pantry staple used in cooking, especially for soups. It is suitable for both meat and vegetarian dishes, making it a convenient dried food item.

Free Talk

The Debate Between Sweet and Salty 262

— Lin Huiyin

A likes to eat sweet, B likes to eat salty.

Because A likes to eat sweet, A says how delicious sweet is, how beneficial it is to eat, and how elegant or magnificent it is to eat. Others who also like to eat sweet echo A's theories, doctrines, or ideologies, and thus become the A faction. B becomes the B faction for the same reasons.

Since there can only be one dominant doctrine, A wants to overthrow B, and B also wants to overthrow A: thus, the debate begins. This is a debate where both the sweet and salty factions believe that their own doctrine should be dominant.

There is also a type of debate where one of the factions does not believe that their own doctrine should be dominant, and even believes that the other faction's doctrine should be dominant, just as that faction believes itself.

Wouldn't that mean there shouldn't be a debate? But there is.

The A faction likes to eat sweet, but they feel that eating sweet is a mistake and that they should actually eat salty. Therefore, they propose a doctrine of eating both sweet and salty, or eating sweet without forgetting salty, even though they may not like to eat salty, or even be unable to eat salty. But they cannot help but propose it because they see clearly, or think they see clearly, that the salty faction's doctrine will be dominant.

But the salty faction finds this doctrine somewhat perplexing, because if they know they should eat salty, why don't they actually eat salty? Why do they still propose this doctrine of harmonizing sweet and salty? Therefore, the salty faction writes rebuttals, and the sweet faction writes replies. Thus, the debate begins again.

Seeing the failure of that sweet faction, or sweet-salty harmonization faction, those who are sensible and aware of the times, those who eat sweet, all say unanimously that eating sweet is undesirable, a habit of young masters, and that eating salty is what heroes and heroic figures do. Because they think they can secretly eat sweet, they must endorse salty in their writing.

Therefore, all the articles in the world are nothing but endorsements of salty, and the debate between sweet and salty comes to an end forever.

Hope 263

— Lao She

Second Brother, the grand prize is 500,000! If you win, you can be carefree and not have to do anything.

Go to Paris to see the girls,

Eat a Chinese meal in London,

A son of wealth shouldn't take an airplane,

Actually, a steamship is not slow either.

Don't wait for something to happen when it's too late,

It's best to save half and spend half.

Spend the half you carry,

What a romantic life of pleasure;

The half you save will generate interest every year,

Less risky than running a business or farming.

What white terror, what green panic,

With money in your pocket, you don't have to worry about anything.

With just ten dollars as capital,

If you don't buy a lottery ticket, you're a fool!

Buy one ticket, ah, buy another,

Two numbers are always better than just one chance.

The lottery hasn't been drawn yet, the lottery hasn't been drawn yet,

Golden dreams come every night.

If I win, I definitely will win,

A meteoric rise, clutching a big leather bag!

If I don't win; how can I not win?

Look in the mirror and see the joy on my face.

Don't even bother polishing my shoes or washing my clothes,

Advertisement 264

— Yu Min

The advertisement says, "Mr. Chen Wangdao, former professor at Fudan University, comments: The Open-Minded National Language textbooks have exquisite and harmonious illustrations, calligraphy, and writing. The words and lines contain rich suggestive power. The examination of calligraphy lessons and the arrangement of phonetic symbols show painstaking effort."

The Open-Minded National Language textbooks are compiled by Mr. Ye Shaojun.

Indeed, they have some distinctive features, but they also have "shortcomings." When Mr. Chen Wangdao mentions phonetic symbols, we can actually find errors in the pronunciation of the national language in these textbooks. In Book 8, Lesson 3, it is written "馬托車." From the context, it is definitely a car, Motor car, but the word "馬" is pronounced in "National Language" as IY in the rising tone,

not LH. If we follow the Romanization spelling of the "Commonly Used Characters of the National Pronunciation Vocabulary" promulgated by the Ministry of Education last year, then "馬托車" would become Maetuoche, which no one, East or West, North or South, would understand what it is. If we say that the word "馬" should be pronounced according to the Southern accent, then the entire textbook's Beijing pronunciation is annotated with the "standard National Language" pronunciation.

Furthermore, it is very regrettable that there are even grammatical errors in this textbook. In Book 4, Lesson 26: "牆上開朶小紅花，牆下蝸牛去看花：無數花開朶朶紅，一齊笑臉歡迎他。(A small red flower blooms on the wall, snails go to see the flower under the wall: countless flowers bloom red, all smiling to welcome him.)" According to the habits of vernacular grammar, it seems that "開朶" means "開着一朶 (blooming a flower)", so why does the following sentence change to "無數花 (countless flowers)"? These are still occasional "oversights" that are easy to correct.

Speaking of "suggestive power," there is a lesson in Book 8 called "The Poor Man and the Rich Man" (Lesson 5). This is the story:

The poor man asks the rich man for the method of "getting rich." The rich man says, "Everything I have here is stolen." So the poor man goes on a stealing spree, and as a result, he is naturally caught. Three years later, he comes out of prison and scolds the rich man as a "bad guy, I fell for your trick." The rich man's answer is wonderful: "I steal natural things, not other people's things: I plant fields, plow land, quarry stone, fell trees: aren't all these natural things? I stole them, and no one has anything to say. As for the things that people have worked so hard to get, they should only be enjoyed by those people. How can you steal them?"

I think it is necessary to add a lesson after this, saying that after hearing this, the poor man really goes to "plant fields, plow land, quarry stone, fell trees:" but landlords and other people jump out of nowhere and ask him to pay rent and settle accounts. He falls for the trick again. When he goes to ask the rich man again, the rich man will tell him: "I am cultivating my own fields, who told you that you don't have your own land, etc.!" The rich man knows in his heart: the method of getting rich lies in getting others to work for himself. But this is a secret. It can't be revealed. Yes, this lesson must be "supplemented," otherwise the poor man will fall for Mr. Ye's trick.

Free Talk has mentioned the need for concrete criticism of elementary school textbooks. I am just writing a few sentences at random, which cannot be regarded as criticism. Perhaps it is just a little feeling after reading the advertisement; and I still admit that Mr. Ye's textbook is comparatively good already.

Homesickness 265

— Tang Zhang

When people are in adversity, they subconsciously think of the people they love and the things they cherish. Travelers in the desert yearn for water and grass, sailors yearn for land, and similarly, in the desolation and boredom of a lodging, one thinks of their hometown and feels homesick. I left my hometown when I was twelve years old, and it has been almost ten years since. During this time, I have experienced much hardship, and my childlike heart has not yet changed. Sometimes I still say a few silly things that "righteous gentlemen" cannot understand.

In recent years, the society I have come into contact with has gradually grown larger; the impression of treachery and violence stabs my chest! I do not have the heart to shrink back and retreat. I have prepared my flesh and blood to bear the hardships of the times! But whenever I wake up in the middle of the night and think of everything in my hometown, I am confused! This is homesickness.

Old Man Qiming said that his affection for his hometown is due to the fact that he "fishes here and roams here." Although there are many things in my hometown that I am attached to, I do not have the idea of "returning home, wearing a kerchief, sitting on a basket, and resting my head on a high pillow to watch the mountain scenery." The reason why I am homesick is actually somewhat similar to Li Chunke's mood of exchanging sable fur for wine and writing in the Beijing residence after drinking. His words are:

"I plan to return! Considering the officialdom and reputation of Chang'an, that's all it is. A bustling group of white-necked crows, their nonsense is considered scholarly. It's hard to remember the names of your kind. I just feel like I don't recognize anyone I meet. Where can I find a confidant in the world? It's just me and myself, dealing with each other. There is no place here to get drunk. Even if it's like being a brave warrior, how many are left today? Three bushels of thorns in my chest, everywhere they grow thorns; everything is unsatisfactory. What is the point of comparing Wu Wenzhong, Sui Luwu, and others to the Bronze Bird Terrace? Who is strong? Duke Xi?

Adversity can certainly be endured, and strength can also be resisted, but white-necked birds are difficult to endure! Even if the Thunder God hits monsters and hits a latrine, he can't help but cover his nose and leave!

As for saying that I don't recognize anyone I meet, that's even more true. Everything in the city is full of strangers; their actions, words, and behaviors are all beyond my understanding. They laugh, laughing at things that I don't think are funny; they scold, scolding people that I don't think deserve to be scolded. If they are the ones holding onto the times, then I am running against the times.

I am tired of seeing these ugly types. I need a pure and simple rural life to adjust my taste and wash away the stench of the city!

I am suffering from homesickness.

Letter to the Editor 266

Dear Editor:

Today I saw a news item in a certain newspaper titled "Another War Against Li is About to Break Out," which involves me, claiming that Free Talk has also severely attacked me, so these attacked writers are uniting to confront Li, etc. There are two points here that must be brought to the attention of the readers: First, my thoughts and personality have their own standpoints. The writers listed in the aforementioned newspaper naturally include some with good thoughts and personalities, but that doesn't mean they are ideological resonance with me. Second, Free Talk has never attacked me, and I am very confident that I will never be attacked by Free Talk. A few days ago, the author of "Reading Notes," Little Snow, had an article with misunderstandings about my poems and poetry talks, but it was very polite and theoretical research, and cannot be considered an attack. Please publish this letter to avoid misunderstandings among friends. Finally, I would like to add that any literary lackeys who are not loyal to their principles, playing jokes on me in some tabloid or boring news, is like "ants trying to shake a tree" or "throwing dung on Buddha's head," causing me no harm! Lin Gengbai, August 6, 1933

Talking Points

Discussing the Way Out for Intellectuals 268

— Bai Bi

Bumping into walls everywhere, where to find a way out? "Looking at the future, I shiver from the cold!"

This is the cry of an intellectual who has been unemployed for a long time, wasted his efforts, and let time pass in vain, deeply stimulated and still without a way to make a living.

Because there is an "oversupply" of knowledge, intellectuals have nowhere to "sell" their knowledge, so a large number of intellectuals become unemployed. In the wave of unemployment, intellectuals are bumping into walls everywhere.

"Where is the way out for intellectuals?" This is a serious problem at the moment. I believe that the first thing to do is to break their traditional ideas of "knowledge is omnipotent" and "character is noble," and to change direction and start from physical labor or productive work. Men might as well become "waiters" or the like, and women might as well become "amah" or the like. But in the current situation of "narrowing market," I also doubt whether my method is effective!

"So where exactly is the way out for intellectuals?" I also thought of the "unintelligent" desperadoes, who are already unemployed. They have already experienced the misfortune that intellectuals are experiencing now. When they are panicked about their livelihoods, their way out is to "steal some" and "rob some"! It is said that they are just going to "steal and return" and "rob and return"! But in the "order of current society," I dare not teach intellectuals to do things that "lose personality" and "commit crimes"!

Therefore, the surplus intellectuals in the current society are finally "without a way out"! Although their "cries" are resounding all around, what is the use of "cries"!

A-Ju, she thought of A-Ju, that little maid's mouth does not have medicine to eat and she chatters, give her the cheongsam.

Miss Three smiled leisurely, Little Xu's strong wrist tempting her in front of her.

A layer of angry frost covered Miss Zhu's sunset face. The car was speeding wildly, the chauffeur looked at his watch, he had to go to the Sanjiang Hotel at nine o'clock.

Robbery 270

— Xiangyun

"Old Wang! Is something wrong?" Fufu was frantically rummaging through

the chest when he suddenly realized an unusual sound coming from afar as a car stopped: honking sounds, followed by a series of leather shoe thuds. He stopped working, pricked up his ears, and seriously lowered his voice, saying:

"Yes!"

Wang Xiaosi shrewdly glanced out the window, saw several figures, separated and moving under the desolate streetlights, mingled with swaying tree shadows. He spoke while stuffing what he had in his hands into his pockets, pulled out the six-inch Browning pistol from his waist, disengaged the safety, and held it tightly in his palm. In the silent world, the thudding of leather shoes, scattered and gradually growing louder.

"Fufu!" Li Desheng, responsible for monitoring the homeowner, stealthily lowered his footsteps and appeared at the stairwell. He said nervously, "Something's up, everyone downstairs!" As soon as Li Desheng finished speaking, he turned and went downstairs. Fufu turned off the light in quick succession and followed Wang Xiaosi down the stairs from the darkness. At the bottom of the stairs, Little Pockmark and Er'er guarded the closed back door, they gripped their Mauser pistols, while directing their bright eyes at those coming downstairs. Reflected in the pale and flickering flashlight, their purplish-blue faces conveyed a determined sense of sacrifice created by the terrifying and dangerous situation. They all clenched their teeth tightly. Their whole bodies trembled as if assailed by the cold wind that pierces the bones. "Go!" Wang Xiaosi turned his head towards everyone and said. His mouth was twitching.

"Yes!"

"Go up and we'll talk later!"

In the dark, Wang Xiaosi saw them all nod their heads slightly,

"Like this: If you die, Er'er, Little Pockmark, with your equipment, charge forward first, Fufu and Lao Li in the back." With a bang, Wang Xiaosi jumped out of the opened door, and immediately fired at the dark figure hiding in the corner of the wall ahead. Behind him, Er'er and Little Pockmark also jumped out. They all kept their bodies close to the wall as they advanced. They tried their best to hide in the darkness. They were all firing bullets cruelly. The crackling sound and the howling of bullets in the room like a raging wind enveloped them. They were hit by bullets, soaked in blood, but they were still struggling, advancing, quickening their pace.

Because of this disturbance, this howling of flying bullets, the residents nearby also trembled and fell into a state of terror and confusion. But suddenly, everything became silent again. The tree shadows still silently leaked light, swaying on the asphalt road, the green wind knocking against the leaves emitted a cool groan, deeply touching people's hearts.

Page 22

A Sworn Brotherhood Remembrance Picture 271

It was four years ago.

Chao Ming and Ying Lin, wanting to deepen their friendship as classmates and become sworn brothers, was of course a very ordinary small matter, nothing rare.

In order to emulate Liu Bei, Guan Yu, and Zhang Fei's Oath of the Peach Garden, they felt that two people forming a sworn brotherhood was a bit awkward, so they hurriedly found a good classmate, Yu Zhang, to fill the gap.

"Sharing blessings and enduring hardships together"; the sworn brotherhood certificate was clearly printed with eight red characters, they took photos, drank wine, and the procedures were considered complete. Based on age, Yu Zhang was the eldest brother, Ying Lin the second brother, and Chao Ming the third brother. Afterwards, it seemed like everyone was very friendly, living happily.

Gradually, they discovered that the second brother was a bit shy and unwilling to tell the truth about things.

"Second brother, be honest, we're all family now": The third brother couldn't keep things to himself. He couldn't help but advise him every time.

"Oh::" The second brother always had this tone.

":::" The eldest brother remained silent.

Fortunately, the second brother gradually reduced his shyness by more than half.

The second brother was a day student, while the eldest and third brothers lived in the school, so they had more contact time.

One day, the third brother was learning to ride a bicycle on the school's sports field. Because it was his first time, he swayed unsteadily. In a panic, the bicycle bumped into someone.

"Sorry, he's a beginner and wasn't careful," the eldest brother said a few words to the other party in a spirit of mutual apology to smooth things over.

"After all, I'm willing to help you, otherwise, humph: : I'm afraid you would have suffered!" The eldest brother boasted proudly afterwards, a trace of complacent smile hanging on his lips.

"Is this something to make a fuss about, who cares": The third brother finally couldn't bear it.

For more than four years, they persevered through this lack of mutual understanding. What continued to arrive was their final semester of senior year in high school.

The relationship between the eldest and third brothers became increasingly fractured! One was arrogant, the other was upright, irreconcilable like water and fire, but due to the constraints of the treaty! The sworn brotherhood certificate! They had to let the pain strike their hearts, no one had the courage to propose severing ties first. As for the second brother, he was just a bit gentle and did not thoroughly understand everything about the sworn brotherhood, only increasing the distance between the three of them, without any major obstacles.

But after all, the mask is just a mask, and it will be torn off one day.

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy

Painting by Mr. Zhang Shuhou of Shouzhou (Brief Biography) 272

Mr. Zhang Shuhou of Shouzhou is an old celebrity from Huainan. With cold eyes, he has witnessed the vicissitudes of life and is nearly seventy years old. There are few old dignitaries of Xiangyang left. Literary people in chaotic times are destined to be withered and starving. Mr. Xiao Shan's hermitage is still in the human world, and the great elegant Qingyou comes again on the sea with a cane. The Master is immersed in the eight laws, meticulously studies seal cutting, and writes the heart of an old horse lying down with the hand of a dragon slaver turning the sea over. His art is close to the Dao.

Under the Red and Green Lights (Forty-Eight) 273

— Xilin

(Twenty-Six) Zhou Shaoping's Last Letter

"Here is a letter from Zhou Shaoping to you!"

"Did he move to another hospital?" he asked, as the letter was placed in his hand.

"He died after the surgery." The nurse replied expressionlessly and walked away.

Shi Qiao was stunned for a long time, as if a light had suddenly flashed and gone out, blurring his vision. When he took the letter to a quiet place and opened it, he managed to focus his vision, regain a sense of reality, and at the same time felt a gust of cold wind blowing from the street corner. The letter trembled;

"Shi Qiao, my dear friend: I only woke up after you left, and I only realized that you had been accompanying me all the way to the hospital. At around three o'clock in the afternoon, the doctor came to perform the operation. The pain was excruciating, but the bullet still hadn't been removed. According to the doctor, the bullet went in very deep, only an inch away from the lungs. Judging from the expression on his face, I probably have no hope. I fainted from the pain again and again. Now he has given me a heart stimulant, so I can barely hold on. Fortunately, the bullet is stuck under my left armpit, giving me this last chance to write to you. This can be considered very lucky.

My sincere brother Shi Qiao, when a soldier who sacrifices for patriotism is about to die, you can imagine that he always wants to say some impassioned words to encourage his compatriots, or leave gentle and reminiscent words to his parents and children, but I feel that the impassioned emotions have come to an end. This is not because of my weakness and discouragement at death; I also feel that it is unnecessary to just reminisce about parents, and it is not because I am inherently vicious and have no filial piety. It's just that I think that under the current chaotic situation in China, the gentle hometown will eventually be completely destroyed, and a simple spirit of passion is definitely not enough to save ourselves and the country. When I was on the front lines, because my comrades were fighting bravely against the enemy, I didn't want to bring up any fundamental national issues for discussion, as discussion during wartime is most likely to scatter military morale. So I have always hidden the problems I have experienced in my heart. Now I know that I have no hope, at this time, let the words filling my heart flow out. Now I might as well honestly say that this time, my participation in the front line battle was not very happy, in other words, there were many psychological contradictions! First of all, in the army organization and the personnel themselves, the flaws I found were simply unbearable. Those I approached on the front lines were mostly soldiers, but in the lives of the soldiers, I saw a deep gap between them and their superiors. It is normal for superiors to have higher salaries, but during combat, superiors take good care of themselves and are unwilling to die. As for the newspapers, naturally, they are all promoting the superiors, especially this time, the comfort items and money given to the front lines by the rear, this is entirely a little comfort that we exchanged for our blood and sweat, heads, but all of it goes to the superiors layer by layer , to be cut off... The question is, they dare to be angry but dare not speak, although they are still driven by patriotism, they still step forward to take orders.
